--- Commit Message ---
LU-12645 tests: Add read ahead tests

The existing readahead tests are too lenient, not checking
misses at all.  They also do not cover enough cases, and
use a complex special purpose utility, which takes in to
account stripe size, etc.  This is overly complex and not
really correct - strided read patterns don't have to have
any relation to stripe size.

Instead, we can just modify multiop to support writing or
reading a certain number of times, optionally jumping
between each operation.  This allows describing any
possible strided pattern with just four arguments -
iterations, size, jump, and starting offset.  (It's also
possible to use this for backwards reads.)

This patch uses multiop to add a short but strict & varied
set of tests for sequential and strided readahead.  It
also simplifies/replaces many of the existing readahead
tests, which did odd things like disable the cache on the
server, which is irrelevant to client side readahead.

Test-Parameters: trivial
Signed-off-by: Patrick Farrell <pfarrell@whamcloud.com>
Signed-off-by: Wang Shilong <wshilong@ddn.com>

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-08-13 15:38:59.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

Thanks for refreshing...

"misses=2 here is not always true for stripe file.
Because for second and later stripe object, read lock will be missed for first time.
So the missing rate ideally should be 2 + stripe count -  1"

I think we should fix this :D
Specifically, if I understand right, I think you're saying readahead will stop and not request a lock.  Is that correct?  If so, I think readahead *should* request a lock.

There is an idea sometimes that readahead is sort of "optional" or "not a priority" and so it shouldn't do certain things...  But readahead is actually the main way pages get read in, and I think we should let it do whatever is needed, within reason.  (Async readahead is a bit of a special case, since it's easy to be too aggressive there... but still.) :)

So I think readahead should request locks if necessary.

Assuming you agree, do you know how to do that?  I bet I can figure it out, but if you already know how...

Patch Set 7:

So we're still failing the strided RA tests when the stride size is small.  Basically, I think because it's counted as "nearby", and so it's not a stride?  (Within 256*PAGE_SIZE I think.)

So a question is:
Do you have an idea for fixing that?  Should we change the tests because it's not really realistic to have such small strides?  I think they will come up but only sometimes...  It would be nicer to make it work for that case if possible..

--- Message (Wang Shilong, 2019-08-22 14:35:24.000000000) ---
Patch Set 7:

> So we're still failing the strided RA tests when the stride size is
 > small.  Basically, I think because it's counted as "nearby", and so
 > it's not a stride?  (Within 256*PAGE_SIZE I think.)
 > 
 > So a question is:
 > Do you have an idea for fixing that?  Should we change the tests
 > because it's not really realistic to have such small strides?  I
 > think they will come up but only sometimes...  It would be nicer to
 > make it work for that case if possible..

Patrick, interesting thing is I could pass tests locally.

Previoulsy, less than 8 page size will not be detected as stride Read.
Instead, it will be detected as sequential read, I think it makes sense in real use case.

I've got some idea to make we support small stride gap too(less than 8K). but now
I'd like to modify tests to make us proceed for now.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-08-22 14:56:53.000000000) ---

OK, that sounds reasonable to me.
